## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: This task belongs to population ecology, as it deals with the growth rate of a population over time, which is a fundamental concept in ecology.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) (density-dependent population growth)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (no carrying capacity, exponential increase)
- Verhulst growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**2) (a more realistic population growth model with carrying capacity)
- Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * t) (population growth with a time-dependent growth rate)
- Population diffusion: dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) (population migration or movement over space)
- Age-structured population model: dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) + c2 * (t ** -c3) (population growth with age-dependent mortality)
- Compensatory growth: dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) + c2 * P**2 (population growth with feedback and self-regulation)
- Baldwin effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 / (P + c2)) (population growth with adaptive traits)
- Carrying capacity model: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (population growth with self-limiting factors)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * ln(c1) * exp(c2 * t) (population growth with non-linear mortality)
- Lotka-Volterra model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P - c2 * t) (population dynamics with predators and prey)
- Hyperbolic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * P) (population growth with non-linear carrying capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Γ¶Ê Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Γ¶Ê Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Γ¶Ê Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Γ¶Ê Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Γ¶Ê Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sigmoidal growth curve Γ¶Ê Logistic growth dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1)
- Growth deceleration Γ¶Ê Verhulst growth dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**2)
- Concave growth Γ¶Ê Gompertz growth dP_dt = c0 * P * ln(c1) * exp(c2 * t)
- Linear decline Γ¶Ê Exponential decay dP_dt = c0 * P
- Bistable dynamics Γ¶Ê Lotka-Volterra model dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P - c2 * t)
- Concave down growth Γ¶Ê Carrying capacity model dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)
- Growth-competition tradeoff Γ¶Ê Compensatory growth dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) + c2 * P**2
- Adaptive traits Γ¶Ê Baldwin effect dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 / (P + c2))
- Mortality dependent on age Γ¶Ê Age-structured population model dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) + c2 * (t ** -c3)
- Complex ecological interactions Γ¶Ê Hyperbolic growth dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * P)

**GT:** `0.11781609251252895*(1 - exp(-0.027228491244958825*P))*P + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

where c0 = c3 Γëê 0.1178, c2 = c4 Γëê 0.02723.

The GT has these basis function components:
1. `P` (linear in P)
2. `P*exp(-c2*P)` (P times exponential in P)
3. `P*exp(-c4*t)` (P times exponential in t)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Key structural requirements:** The GT depends on `t` only through `P*exp(-c4*t)`. Any candidate must be able to reproduce this t-dependence exactly.

### Candidate 1: `P*(c0 + c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(P*c4))`
= `c0*P + c1*P*exp(c2*t) + c3*P*exp(c4*P)`

GT = `c0'*P + c3'*P*exp(-c4'*t) - c0'*P*exp(-c2'*P)`

This has: P, P*exp(c2*t), P*exp(c4*P). Setting c2 negative gives P*exp(-|c2|*t). Setting c4 negative gives P*exp(-|c4|*P). This matches the three basis functions exactly!

- c0*P matches the P term
- c1*P*exp(c2*t) with c2 = -0.02723 matches P*exp(-c4*t)
- c3*P*exp(c4*P) with c4 = -0.02723 matches -c0*P*exp(-c2*P)

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidates 2-50: t-dependence analysis

Most candidates use `log(c2*t + 1)` for t-dependence. Since `log(c2*t + 1)` is NOT equivalent to `exp(-c4*t)` (they are fundamentally different functions - logarithmic vs exponential), these cannot match unless the log terms can be zeroed out AND there's another mechanism for the exp(-t) dependence.

Let me check which candidates have `exp(c*t)` terms or can zero out log terms while providing exp(-t) dependence:
